The agent can then poll the log to see the status of its request.•Files I Am Building:•/home/ubuntu/human-ai/skills/env_request_manager/•/home/ubuntu/human-ai/skills/env_request_manager/__init__.py•/home/ubuntu/human-ai/skills/env_request_manager/env_request_manager_skill.py• (The skill will contain the logic to write requests, read responses, and manage the log securely).🔧 How I Am Using the Swarm to Assist MyselfWhile I am the primary developer of this skill, I amnot working in isolation. 23:42TheNotebookLM-Debuggerhas completed its investigation, and the root cause of the login failure is now clear.🔍 The Verdict: Google's "Security Wall"The failure isn't due to a bug in our code, but rather two specific issues:1.Missing Credentials: The current.envfiles only contain placeholders for the Google email and password.2.Bot Detection: Google aggressively blocks automated login attempts (filling email/password via script), usually throwing a "This browser or app may not be secure" error.🛠️ The Solution: Session-Based AuthenticationTrying to automate the login process is a losing battle with Google. To fix this permanently and maintain our "Browser-Only" architecture, we need to shift to aSession-Based Authmodel.The Plan:1.Manual Handshake: You will need to run thelogin_helper.pyscriptoncein a headed browser. This allows you to log in manually, handle any 2FA, and save a fully authenticated session profile to the disk.2.Headless Persistence: Once that session is saved, theNotebookLMAgentwill simply load that profile. It will effectively "wake up" already logged in, bypassing the login screen entirely.3.Session Health Check: I will update the agent to verify the dashboard is present before starting. If the session expires, the agent will notify you to re-run the helper rather than trying (and failing) to log in automatically.Action Required:When you have a moment, please run the following command in your terminal to authenticate the session:python3 /home/ubuntu/human-ai/core/agents/notebook_lm/login_helper.pyOnce you've completed the login in the browser window that opens, let me know, and I'll trigger the agent to start its tasks! 🚀

00:34CdreamerLook at the following repo and how it can improve the browser agents “https://github.com/browser-use/browser-harness”
00:34Openclaw25_botThis repository is a goldmine for exactly what we are trying to achieve with the Navigator Agent. While our current agent is a "Generalist" (relying on the LLM to figure everything out),browser-harnessprovides aDomain-Specific Skill Layer.Here is how we can integrate these concepts to supercharge our browser agents:1. The "Domain-Skill" ArchitectureThe most valuable part of this repo is the/domain-skillsdirectory. Instead of asking the LLM to "figure out how to search Amazon," we can implementPre-defined Skill Modules.•The Improvement: We can create aDomainSkillclass. When the Navigator Agent detects it is onamazon.comorgithub.com, it loads the corresponding.mdor.pyskill.•Result: This drastically reduces the "Reasoning" load on the LLM, eliminates the "I don't know where the search bar is" errors, and makes the agent 10x faster and more reliable on common sites.2. Advanced Interaction PrimitivesOur current agent has basicclickandfill.browser-harnesshas a specialized/interaction-skillslibrary that handles the "hard" parts of the web:•Shadow DOM: Many modern sites (including Google) use Shadow DOM, which standard Playwright selectors can't see. Integrating theirshadow-dom.mdlogic will stop the "Selector not found" errors.•Cross-Origin Iframes: Essential for handling payment gateways or embedded login windows.•Profile Sync: Theirprofile-sync.mdprovides a better blueprint for how we handle the authenticated Chromium profiles we just set up.3. The "Harness" Concept (Daemonization)They use adaemon.pyandadmin.pyapproach. Instead of spawning a fresh browser for every task (which is slow and triggers bot detection), they maintain apersistent browser daemon.•The Improvement: We can move theWebNavigatorinto a background service. The agents just send "instructions" to the daemon.•Result: Instant execution, better session persistence, and significantly lower resource overhead.🚀 Integration PlanI propose we implement a"Hybrid Skill-Based Navigator":1.Phase 1: Interaction Upgrade: I'll integrate theShadow DOMandIframehandlers frombrowser-harnessinto ourWebNavigatorclass.2.Phase 2: Domain Layer: I'll create adomain_skills/folder in our repo. For the first test, I'll implement thegoogleandgithubskills based on their patterns.3.Phase 3: Daemonization: I'll explore moving the browser control to a background process to eliminate the "Profile in Use" lock errors we hit earlier.Shall I start by implementing the Shadow DOM and Iframe support to make the Navigator more robust?
